          <div class="columns-inner">
           <div class="column-center-outer">
            <div class="column-center-inner">
             <div class="main section" id="main" name="Main">
              <div class="widget Blog" id="Blog1">
               <div class="blog-posts hfeed">
                <!-- google_ad_section_start(name=default) -->
                <div class="date-outer">
                 <h2 class="date-header">
                  <span>
                   Wednesday, August 8, 2007
                  </span>
                 </h2>
                 <div class="date-posts">
                  <div class="post-outer">
                   <div class="post hentry" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
                    <meta content="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/SWJjTcIaCMI/AAAAAAAAAUQ/Lh3d0enCncU/s400/wrapper1.jpg" itemprop="image_url"/>
                    <meta content="2557554237845668577" itemprop="blogId"/>
                    <meta content="2212653623360428858" itemprop="postId"/>
                    <a name="2212653623360428858">
                    </a>
                    <h3 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name">
                     chip wrapper purse instructions
                    </h3>
                    <div class="post-header">
                     <div class="post-header-line-1">
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-2212653623360428858" itemprop="description articleBody">
                     <a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/SWJjTcIaCMI/AAAAAAAAAUQ/Lh3d0enCncU/s1600-h/wrapper1.jpg">
                      <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5287898098106501314" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/SWJjTcIaCMI/AAAAAAAAAUQ/Lh3d0enCncU/s400/wrapper1.jpg" style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN: 0px auto 10px; WIDTH: 400px; CURSOR: hand; HEIGHT: 300px; TEXT-ALIGN: center"/>
                     </a>
                     <br/>
                     <div>
                      <a href="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsDMBoYeS3I/AAAAAAAAAAc/ufwiw7M2Dg8/s1600-h/purse2.jpg">
                      </a>
                      Cut each potato chip bag into 2 X 4 1/2  pieces. Using a rotary cutter makes it fast. I use potato chip bags, cookie packages, ramen noodle packages, anything really. I've tried some heavy plastics but they are hard to slide into each other, they want to stick. With the large potato chip bags it only takes about 20 bags to make a whole purse. (I think, don't quote me on that, that's what I tried to figure out one time.
                      <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5287898412306497698" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/SWJjlunhgKI/AAAAAAAAAUY/KpdpgMjM-x4/s400/wrapper3.jpg" style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN: 0px auto 10px; WIDTH: 400px; CURSOR: hand; HEIGHT: 300px; TEXT-ALIGN: center"/>
                      <br/>
                      Cut magazine pages the same size as each chip bag piece. Each piece you fold will have a piece of magazine paper in it to make it very sturdy. You do not have to have paper in each piece when you fold, the difference is the thickness of the finished bag.  I've made plenty without the paper inside and you can't tell the difference.
                     </div>
                     <div>
                      Folding instructions for each piece can be found at www.gumwrapper.com/build.htm .. start with #3 on the instruction sheet because your pieces are already cut to size.
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsDhlIYeTBI/AAAAAAAAABs/hEes_yE6fEY/s1600-h/4.jpg">
                      </a>
                      <br/>
                      Once you have 60 wrapper pieces together you need to join them into a circle.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsIHyoYeTdI/AAAAAAAAAFQ/yU_xgeZL3uk/s1600-h/4.jpg">
                      </a>
                      <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5287922575545875874" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/SWJ5kNsuPaI/AAAAAAAAAU4/Dmm1SeIOaLs/s320/wrapper2.jpg" style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN: 0px auto 10px; WIDTH: 320px; CURSOR: hand; HEIGHT: 240px; TEXT-ALIGN: center"/>
                      Take the first wrapper piece off and put into the other side by unfolding and putting the raw edges into the last chain (green piece in photo)
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsDyJIYeTEI/AAAAAAAAACI/yxVPdLhXPng/s1600-h/7.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098341016866278466" src="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsDyJIYeTEI/AAAAAAAAACI/yxVPdLhXPng/s200/7.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsDyIIYeTCI/AAAAAAAAAB4/02GYNor8xHI/s1600-h/5.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098340999686409250" src="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsDyIIYeTCI/AAAAAAAAAB4/02GYNor8xHI/s200/5.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsDyI4YeTDI/AAAAAAAAACA/3xVEELgGqU8/s1600-h/6.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098341012571311154" src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsDyI4YeTDI/AAAAAAAAACA/3xVEELgGqU8/s200/6.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsDyI4YeTDI/AAAAAAAAACA/3xVEELgGqU8/s1600-h/6.jpg">
                      </a>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Follow the pictures........it's like your making the chain backwards.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsD0oYYeTFI/AAAAAAAAACQ/Gyj2fn6MZMA/s1600-h/8.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098343752760446034" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsD0oYYeTFI/AAAAAAAAACQ/Gyj2fn6MZMA/s200/8.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsD0o4YeTGI/AAAAAAAAACY/ijPXcgYW5vY/s1600-h/9.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098343761350380642" src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsD0o4YeTGI/AAAAAAAAACY/ijPXcgYW5vY/s200/9.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsD0pYYeTHI/AAAAAAAAACg/Hwa2Uz6bz0U/s1600-h/10.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098343769940315250" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsD0pYYeTHI/AAAAAAAAACg/Hwa2Uz6bz0U/s200/10.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div align="center">
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div align="left">
                       <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsD1vYYeTII/AAAAAAAAACo/oT_mRQX1yio/s1600-h/11.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098344972531158146" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsD1vYYeTII/AAAAAAAAACo/oT_mRQX1yio/s200/11.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsD1v4YeTJI/AAAAAAAAACw/8fmkPG-KJr0/s1600-h/12.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098344981121092754" src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsD1v4YeTJI/AAAAAAAAACw/8fmkPG-KJr0/s200/12.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       I have to use a screw driver or something flat to push the
                       <span style="font-size:100%;">
                        piece
                       </span>
                       down into the chain. Tuck the raw edges into the previous wrapper so it looks like the other wrappers in the chain.
                      </div>
                      <div align="center">
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div align="center">
                       <span style="font-size:130%;color:#ff0000;">
                        SEWING ROWS TOGETHER
                       </span>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div align="left">
                       Each wrapper pice has has like a positive and negative on each side if you are looking down on top of the row. You will be fitting a positive against a negative so when you sew the rows together you have a continues up/down sewing motion.
                      </div>
                      <div align="left">
                       <span style="color:#ff0000;">
                        photo of positive edge                    photo of negative edge
                       </span>
                      </div>
                      <div align="center">
                       <span style="font-size:130%;color:#ff0000;">
                        <a href="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEAUYYeTLI/AAAAAAAAADA/d16zzyQTSSY/s1600-h/14.jpg">
                         <img alt="" border="0" height="208" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098356603302595762" src="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEAUYYeTLI/AAAAAAAAADA/d16zzyQTSSY/s320/14.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; WIDTH: 252px; CURSOR: hand; HEIGHT: 149px" width="246"/>
                        </a>
                       </span>
                      </div>
                      <div align="center">
                       <a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RstnraQ1KtI/AAAAAAAAAHY/3Ky-U8cYRaI/s1600-h/13.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101284998409169618" src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RstnraQ1KtI/AAAAAAAAAHY/3Ky-U8cYRaI/s200/13.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div align="center">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div align="center">
                       <span style="font-size:130%;color:#ff0000;">
                        <a href="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEAUYYeTLI/AAAAAAAAADA/d16zzyQTSSY/s1600-h/14.jpg">
                        </a>
                       </span>
                      </div>
                      <div align="center">
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div align="left">
                       <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsESzIYeTMI/AAAAAAAAADI/dw922GiQ0OA/s1600-h/15.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098376922792873154" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsESzIYeTMI/AAAAAAAAADI/dw922GiQ0OA/s320/15.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       You can use a large eyes needle with a blunt tipto sew the rows together or make yourself a needle out of a credit card or some type of heavy plastic.  Poke a hole in one end for the needle to tie your thread on.  Just a strong knot will be fine. The size of the piece of credit card was cut 2 3/8 X 1/2. That seemed to work the best but you will need a needle to attach the zipper. I
                       <span class="blsp-spelling-error" id="SPELLING_ERROR_2">
                        ve
                       </span>
                       tried several different kind of thread..I dont know that there is a wrong or right thread..as long as it is very strong. The thread that I was using in the photos was a denim jean thread. Its very strong and wont break but it was so thin that it actually was like a knife and cut my wrapper.
                       <span class="blsp-spelling-error" id="SPELLING_ERROR_3">
                        DMC
                       </span>
                       floss worked fine, I found a doily crochet thread that worked. I checked into the fishing line that everyone talks about, it was catfish nylon and would not break but I cant find any thin enough. Its all just to thick. I
                       <span class="blsp-spelling-error" id="SPELLING_ERROR_8">
                        ve
                       </span>
                       read lots of info of speculation on how these purses are put together..they are all sewn and NOT woven or folded together.  I also light to use baby crochet yarn.  It's a great thickness and won't break when it's pulled tight.
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div align="left">
                       To begin sewing rows together.bring needle up
                       <span class="blsp-spelling-error" id="SPELLING_ERROR_9">
                        thru
                       </span>
                       any chain and back down the other side and tie a strong knot. (next 3 photos) You will weave your loose thread ends into the purse later. The beginning is the only time that you will tie your thread onto the purse. As you run out of thread, tie on with a square knot and continue sewing
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div align="center">
                       <br/>
                       <a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEYZ4YeTQI/AAAAAAAAADo/iGwTbgyUGqo/s1600-h/16.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098383086070942978" src="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEYZ4YeTQI/AAAAAAAAADo/iGwTbgyUGqo/s200/16.jpg" style="CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEYaIYeTRI/AAAAAAAAADw/YWo-4R6Gpsc/s1600-h/17.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098383090365910290" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEYaIYeTRI/AAAAAAAAADw/YWo-4R6Gpsc/s200/17.jpg" style="CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEYaIYeTSI/AAAAAAAAAD4/pVfvD68gIV0/s1600-h/18.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098383090365910306" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEYaIYeTSI/AAAAAAAAAD4/pVfvD68gIV0/s200/18.jpg" style="CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       Put two chains together as I described with the positive and negative. You will be sewing down
                       <span class="blsp-spelling-error" id="SPELLING_ERROR_10">
                        thru
                       </span>
                       a chain, over slightly to the right and down
                       <span class="blsp-spelling-error" id="SPELLING_ERROR_11">
                        thru
                       </span>
                       the next chain, up
                       <span class="blsp-spelling-error" id="SPELLING_ERROR_12">
                        thru
                       </span>
                       the next chain and down
                       <span class="blsp-spelling-error" id="SPELLING_ERROR_13">
                        thru
                       </span>
                       the next one. Follow the picturesYou will continue to do this until you get all the way around to where you began sewing.
                      </div>
                      <div align="center">
                       <br/>
                       <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEdnIYeTVI/AAAAAAAAAEQ/iw9RegBz7BI/s1600-h/19.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098388811262348626" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEdnIYeTVI/AAAAAAAAAEQ/iw9RegBz7BI/s200/19.jpg" style="CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <a href="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEdnYYeTWI/AAAAAAAAAEY/81IiUoJWxDw/s1600-h/20.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098388815557315938" src="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEdnYYeTWI/AAAAAAAAAEY/81IiUoJWxDw/s200/20.jpg" style="CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <a href="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEgRYYeTbI/AAAAAAAAAFA/4kfI_SJiTXg/s1600-h/21.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098391736135077298" src="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEgRYYeTbI/AAAAAAAAAFA/4kfI_SJiTXg/s200/21.jpg" style="CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEgRoYeTcI/AAAAAAAAAFI/JZ0zuoGqSAI/s1600-h/22.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5098391740430044610" src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsEgRoYeTcI/AAAAAAAAAFI/JZ0zuoGqSAI/s200/22.jpg" style="CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div align="left">
                       <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsWi1aQ1KiI/AAAAAAAAAGA/npQNjqfJaFM/s1600-h/25.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5099661191533636130" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsWi1aQ1KiI/AAAAAAAAAGA/npQNjqfJaFM/s200/25.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                      </div>
                      <div align="center">
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       Continue sewing in an up and down motion until you go all the way around. Make sure you pull the thread tight so you do not have any gaps or see the thread.
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <div align="left">
                       <br/>
                       Once you go all the way around, you need to run your thread over the top of the purse rows to sew the other side of the purse. You will be sewing the inside and the ourside of your purse. Your purse will become very stiff as you  pull the thread tight when sewing the chains together
                       <br/>
                       <span style="color:#cc0000;">
                        photo showing running the thread over the top row to sew the other side of the purse.
                       </span>
                      </div>
                      <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5099663923132836418" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsWlUaQ1KkI/AAAAAAAAAGQ/MfIkOJaPL24/s200/26.jpg" style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN: 0px auto 10px; CURSOR: hand; TEXT-ALIGN: center"/>
                      <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsWkLaQ1KjI/AAAAAAAAAGI/OvUA8V38WmQ/s1600-h/27.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5099662669002385970" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsWkLaQ1KjI/AAAAAAAAAGI/OvUA8V38WmQ/s200/27.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div align="left">
                      </div>
                      add the next row.......remember to position positive to negative
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div align="left">
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <span style="font-size:130%;color:#ff0000;">
                        SEWING THE BOTTOM
                       </span>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div align="center">
                       <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/Rsth_6Q1KmI/AAAAAAAAAGg/NF2kbfSi4RA/s1600-h/31.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101278753526721122" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/Rsth_6Q1KmI/AAAAAAAAAGg/NF2kbfSi4RA/s200/31.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <a href="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RstiAKQ1KnI/AAAAAAAAAGo/0jRp_zfhdyE/s1600-h/29.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101278757821688434" src="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RstiAKQ1KnI/AAAAAAAAAGo/0jRp_zfhdyE/s200/29.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RstiAqQ1KoI/AAAAAAAAAGw/DnMp6CQaQT0/s1600-h/30.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101278766411623042" src="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RstiAqQ1KoI/AAAAAAAAAGw/DnMp6CQaQT0/s200/30.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div align="center">
                       <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RstiA6Q1KpI/AAAAAAAAAG4/dZ0fiIntTuw/s1600-h/32.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101278770706590354" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RstiA6Q1KpI/AAAAAAAAAG4/dZ0fiIntTuw/s200/32.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                      </div>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Squeeze the bottom together and start sewing. You will only be able to sew the outside of this row. There is not enough room on the inside of the purse to sew like you did on the other rows.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div align="left">
                      </div>
                      <br/>
                      I can't really explain how to sew the bottom, but once you squeeze it together just start running your needle thru the rows to hold them together. It doesn't matter how many times you go around a square because you will never see the thread. The only place that you can see my thread is in the very corners. You will have to sew around the corners a couple of times to pull them tight. The bottom is harder to have a consistant sewing pattern because your sewing the positive to positive. You'll totally understand what I'm talking about once you begin sewing. :-)
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RstiBaQ1KqI/AAAAAAAAAHA/QyHk6ZOwul8/s1600-h/36.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101278779296524962" src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RstiBaQ1KqI/AAAAAAAAAHA/QyHk6ZOwul8/s200/36.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <span style="font-size:85%;">
                       Continue sewing along the bottom.  You will be tucking in one wrapper square at each corner.   Once you get it tucked in,  it's not going anywhere because it's so tightly wedged in to the corner.
                       <br/>
                      </span>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div align="left">
                      </div>
                      <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101281910327683762" src="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/Rstk3qQ1KrI/AAAAAAAAAHI/cH_gYXG_aXg/s320/37.jpg" style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN: 0px auto 10px; CURSOR: hand; TEXT-ALIGN: center"/>
                      <br/>
                      <span style="font-size:180%;color:#ff0000;">
                       ADDING THE ZIPPER
                      </span>
                      <div align="left">
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                       <a href="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsycE6Q1KvI/AAAAAAAAAHo/X3K_eY2rLUo/s1600-h/43.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101624086077188850" src="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsycE6Q1KvI/AAAAAAAAAHo/X3K_eY2rLUo/s200/43.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsycFaQ1KwI/AAAAAAAAAHw/y7UEPasr_A8/s1600-h/44.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101624094667123458" src="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsycFaQ1KwI/AAAAAAAAAHw/y7UEPasr_A8/s200/44.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <a href="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsycF6Q1KxI/AAAAAAAAAH4/AkCbGrh0HAU/s1600-h/45.jpg">
                        <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101624103257058066" src="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsycF6Q1KxI/AAAAAAAAAH4/AkCbGrh0HAU/s200/45.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                       </a>
                       <br/>
                       <br/>
                      </div>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      Doesn't matter what type of zipper you buy..... just so it is long enough to go across the purse. You will cut the excess off when you are finished sewing onto the purse if it is to long.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsycGKQ1KyI/AAAAAAAAAIA/4xWuBuoUzhM/s1600-h/46.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101624107552025378" src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsycGKQ1KyI/AAAAAAAAAIA/4xWuBuoUzhM/s200/46.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <br/>
                      Catch the very edge of the zipper and then run your needle down thru a chain and up the next one.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsycGKQ1KzI/AAAAAAAAAII/hrI2rHA0pCI/s1600-h/47.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101624107552025394" src="http://bp3.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsycGKQ1KzI/AAAAAAAAAII/hrI2rHA0pCI/s200/47.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      If you look really close at this picture, the needle is running down thru the chain of red wrapper with the yellow strip through it. The needle will come back up through the white chain.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsydBaQ1K0I/AAAAAAAAAIQ/kH5gnotDeJI/s1600-h/48.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101625125459274562" src="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsydBaQ1K0I/AAAAAAAAAIQ/kH5gnotDeJI/s200/48.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      This picture is a little blurry but what I'm trying to show is the needle coming back up the white chain. You will catch the edge of the zipper at every "v" around the chain.
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://bp0.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsydBaQ1K0I/AAAAAAAAAIQ/kH5gnotDeJI/s1600-h/48.jpg">
                      </a>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsydBqQ1K2I/AAAAAAAAAIg/f7TzLkC7wfA/s1600-h/50.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101625129754241890" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsydBqQ1K2I/AAAAAAAAAIg/f7TzLkC7wfA/s200/50.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <br/>
                      Do both ends of the zipper like the picture. It doesn't really matter how long the zipper is because once you tuck the ends inside the purse you can cut the zipper off.
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsydBqQ1K1I/AAAAAAAAAIY/mLhV_EjrSyA/s1600-h/49.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101625129754241874" src="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsydBqQ1K1I/AAAAAAAAAIY/mLhV_EjrSyA/s200/49.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <a href="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsydB6Q1K3I/AAAAAAAAAIo/_nDgZnmX2N0/s1600-h/51.jpg">
                       <img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5101625134049209202" src="http://bp2.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsydB6Q1K3I/AAAAAAAAAIo/_nDgZnmX2N0/s200/51.jpg" style="FLOAT: left; MARGIN: 0px 10px 10px 0px; CURSOR: hand"/>
                      </a>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div align="center">
                       <span style="font-size:180%;color:#ff0000;">
                        <a href="http://bp1.blogger.com/_4yWfJYiJn3g/RsydBqQ1K2I/AAAAAAAAAIg/f7TzLkC7wfA/s1600-h/50.jpg">
                        </a>
                       </span>
                      </div>
                      <br/>
                      <br/>
                      <div align="center">
                       <span style="font-size:180%;color:#ff0000;">
                       </span>
                      </div>
                      <br/>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-5487331841703891481">
                       <p>
                        Thanks so very much for posting the tutorial on the potato chip wrapper purse. I have seen so many folks said they were going to post the instructions for these purses and never did, you are the first on the web (imagine!) to do so. The instructions are clear and easy to understand.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I have been making these purses for about 8 months. I had to buy a purse and study it to learn how to make them. This is truly an art that has so much potential. There is so much to learn but this is a great beginning.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I noticed someone made a very beautiful purse using magazine covers. That should work fine but if you want to make a purse that is water resistant cover each piece of paper form the magazine with storage tape. I use the scotch brand storage tape it seems to work best(less static). The storage tape is almost wide enough to cover the pieces  of paper you are using. Put the piece of paper on a flat surface try to put the tape right down the middle of the paper. Then cut the tape to the size of the length of the paper. When you fold up the paper it ( the outside) should be completely covered by the tape and very strong. I mention this because now that we have good instructions, folks should not have to wait until they get enough potato chip bags or candy wrappers to begin using the information. I look forward to more exciting developments on your blog.
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                       <p>
                        I also made my first purse out of magazine covers since I didn't have enough chip bags and that was my suggestions to nan.  She is covering the outside of hers with puzzle glue and I'm using modge podge to see if we can make them durable.  I'm not so much worried about the water as I am the papers tearing.  I also thought about covering each piece with packing tape but thought it was to much work but if someone else is doing it then maybe I will too.  I understand you instructions to say that you fold the packing tape to the inside.  How does that make is waterproof?  Are you using the regular pages of magazine or only the covers.  I used only the covers to make my first purse since they were stronger than the inside pages.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I'm so excited to hear that there is someone else that has made this purse.  If you have any more ideas or suggestions I would love to know.  Send me a picture and I'll put it up on my page.

                       <p>
                        I've been experimenting with magazine covers and newspapers.  I had too many problems connecting each piece when it measured 2 x 4 so I increased the size to 2 x 4-1/2...it was much easier and doesn't leave any spaces.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I also put packing tape over each piece but don't want to continue with this method because it is very tedious.  Additionally, it makes the purse very thick.  My idea is to make cosmetic bags out of newspapers for Christmas gifts...so I don't want the "material" to be so thick http://www.ecoist.com/newspaper.asp).  I also recently saw them at a store the newspaper ones were very thick...I thought too bulky.  I was just thinking of trying modge podge...please let me know how it works!

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-6679335496085301174">
                       <p>
                        Hello. The storage  tape should wind up being on the outside of the folded piece of paper. This makes the piece of paper very strong and durable and highly water resistant. for this I would use the pages of the magazine not the cover. If there are pictures on the pages that you use, the tape will make them look like beautiful glossy photos. try to use pages that have mostly pictures on them. To see how strong the tape will make each segment cut a piece of storage tape 4 and a half inches long and fold it up(no paper added) as you would the paper segments. Now try to tear it. It will be very hard to do!  Basically you are doing the same thing as you are doing with the candy wrappers. There is a plastic material on the outside of each segment and paper underneath. With the use of the clear tape the picture or pattern will be on the paper not on the plastic.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        As far as the purse being too thick with the tape being placed on the paper, you want your purse to feel strong and durable not flimsy. Tape is not much thicker than the material used in making potato chip bags.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        As far as this being time consuming, this kind of work just takes time!
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-6599657530547624001">
                       <p>
                        Dear Sugar Girl,
                        <br/>
                        My only suggestion on why your chain wouldn't be very strong is that the size of your starting piece that your folding is wrong.  If you use the 2 X 4 1/2 piece and interlock them together it will turn out to be very strong - strong enough to use for a purse handle :-)  good luck.....Mylinda
                       </p>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-5684110607892995021">
                       <p>
                        Dear Purse Pals,
                        <br/>
                        I have not yet made a purse with a flat bottom but I do have some wonderful pictures of one that was sent to me.  My next goal is to make one and believe me......I will post instructions and pictures.  To answer another question......This is what I do.......I cut stacks of chip bags and magazine pages at the same time and have them rubber band together.  That way I can keep a stack of each in my purse to fold when I'm setting someplace and bored.  When I used the magazine cover pages I only needed one piece because it's so thick but on the chip wrappers I have to insert a piece of magazine page to make it thicker.  There is a difference in thickness between magazine cover and pages.
                        <br/>
                        When I made the purse from magazine covers I folded lots at one time and kept them in a basket to connect into chains later but when I'm working with the chip wrappers I add them to the chain as I fold them because they don't stay folded as well.  I have all my girls on my bowling team folding for me.......They all know I've lost it!!!
                        <br/>
                        My little homemade needle for sewing the purses together finally got brittle and broke so if anyone has any other suggestions on what to use I would love for you to share.
                        <br/>
                        Good luck to all......
                        <br/>
                        Mylinda
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-4691586247842606024">
                       <p>
                        The template plastic was my very first try and it didn't last long......so that's when I went to an old credit card because it was thicker......It did last for about 4 purses before it broke.......I just need to get more credit cards....lol.
                        <br/>
                        The way you can mark my page from your blog page to find it easier is to do like what I did with Nan's blog page.  On your blog page...go to customize &gt; template &gt; page element &gt; add a page element &gt; link list &gt; Type in title what it will say on your page and then copy and past my blog address into the URL.
                        <br/>
                        The only way I find my blog page is I have it bookmarked in my favorites on internet explorer.
                        <br/>
                        Hope that helps and I'd be happy to add you to my blog page once your up and running.
                        <br/>
                        Mylinda
                       </p>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-5377686368999443877">
                       <p>

                       <div class="avatar-image-container avatar-stock">
                        <span dir="ltr">
                         <a class="avatar-hovercard" href="http://www.blogger.com/profile/11828139804379141620" id="av-22-11828139804379141620" onclick="" rel="nofollow">

                       said...
                      </dt>
                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-5389132045314956228">
                       <p>
                        Hello Texas gal
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        The thread I use is a #69 Conso thread. The thread (#69 Conso) is black but it comes in many colors. I believe the thread is used also for upholstering furniture. I have a 8 ounce roll of it that I have been using for ten or more years. I usually cut a piece of thread 4 arm lengths long (It is a good idea to  start with a shorter lenght until you get use to using thread) . If I am careful I can use that lenght without getting too many tangles that I have to tease apart. I tie the piece of thread on to the work so that I am working with only 1/2 thread at a time so the whole thread does not get over worked.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I have a question related to your question. has anyone found a good way to keep the thread from tangling up? Most times I do not have a problem but when I get stressed it is like magic the thread seems to get tangled up! I have found that working with a large needle helps. It seems to open the the work up a bit and reduce the wear on the thread. I use size 13 to 16 blunt end tapestry needles. I have tried treating the thread by rubbing it with a dryer sheet to reduce static but that did not seem to help me.
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-1973359880665993083">
                       <p>
                        Here are a few thread detangling tricks.........Can't really say they are tried and true but you might want to give one a try.
                        <br/>
                        1.  Coat your thread with bees wax.
                        <br/>
                        2.  Iron your thread.....it takes the spiral out of the thread.
                        <br/>
                        3.  Thread your needle from the end of thread coming off the spool.  Remember.....the end you cut is the end you knot.
                        <br/>
                        That's the only ones I can remember.
                        <br/>
                        Best of luck
                        <br/>
                        Mylinda
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                       <p>
                        My thread of choice to sew my bags is waxed dental floss.  I know it's not what you were expecting to hear from me is it? The reason? It's flat, it's already waxed, it doesn't knot up as easily and it's strong. All I can say is give it a try and see what you think.

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-3087973723528013102">
                       <p>
                        I am currently making a purse and have found a GREAT source of wrapper-like material.  I went to the dollar store.  They had a whole rack of banners saying things like Happy Birthday etc.  It is the same material as a candy wrapper.  I paid 1 dollar for a five inch by six foot banner.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        The one I choose was a soft yellow with the lettering in different colours and patterns.  It's making up into a beautiful purse.
                       </p>

                       <p>
                        I made a flat bottom purse with camoflage (hunting magazines-cut out everything) covered in mailing tape (storage tape is too thick), sewn with dental floss &amp; bamboo handles. These are very pretty.
                        <br/>
                        Pull the tape - sticky side up, place the paper on the tape, then cut them apart after all pieces are in place.
                        <br/>
                        Thank you for the ideas &amp; help.
                        <br/>
                        Cindy

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-3601417103023690467">
                       <p>
                        Here is the answer to the last 2 posts.  It is not necessary to cover each piece of chip wrapper with tape.  The reason that you cover the magazine paper with tape is to really make it waterproof.  Chip wrappers are already waterproof so there is no need to cover.  You only use a single layer of chip wrapper.  It does make the total stability of the purse thicker if you insert the piece of paper inside the chip wrapper piece before folding.  It is not a must but end result to nicer.
                        <br/>
                        Mylinda
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      </dt>
                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-752849175074054306">
                       <p>
                        Once again, I'm going to try to answer several questions at once. To cover the pieces with tape, go to candywrappercrafts.blogspot.  There are instructions there. There was a questions on where to buy mod pog, go to any craft store or Walmart.
                        <br/>
                        To get the corner pieces to bend in to the center, try fold that particular piece in half with a pair of pliers.  All your really doing when you push that piece to the inside is folding it in half.  See if that helps you.  I have figured out how to make the purse square along the top but not time to get anything written up and posted.  I will post a picture of the belt I made which is a rectangle. See if you can figure out how to make a purse by looking at the belt.
                        <br/>
                        I have not posted the instructions yet to make the pop tab purse.  I started a blog page with the picture but that's all the further I've gotten.
                        <br/>
                        Good luck and happy folding
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-7741326022247700381">
                       <p>
                        Answers to a few more qustions:
                        <br/>
                        To Sara - My purse is 7 rounds with 1 additional round for the handle.  I do have one that is 6 rounds and it's just as cute.
                        <br/>
                        I might suggest, to get you started, to make one of the little coin purses that you see.  You use 28 pieces per row and only 4 rows.  It's made exactly the same as the purse you can just get it done in couple of days verses a week!
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        To Nikki - To Attach the buckle to the belt, I just folded 4 pieces over (or two rows) and sewed with needle and thread.  Good luck
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-2706044792287032260">
                       <p>
                        Just finished my first attempt at this project &amp; wanted to share some of the things I tried.... I used nylon jewelry beading monofilament to sew my wrappers together &amp; this worked well for me. You can get this in different strengths/thicknesses. I didn't have an old credit card, so I used a large paper clip. Worked fine for me.
                        <br/>
                        Also used clear contact paper on large pieces I thought needed extra protection. Does any one know of any reason why this won't work?
                        <br/>
                        Finally, just wanted to let other beginners know that single size M&amp;M wrappers will tear, so cover them with tape first!
                        <br/>
                        This was so much fun, I'm anxious to start another project. Thanks again Mylinda!
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                       <p>
                        hi, thank you for the instructions. I made a purse for my 20 year old daughter with magazine pages covered in tape, using mainly pink green and blue colors, (I found a People magazine on Hannah Montana that was great) I added tiny pictures printed out from my computer and taped them on some of the pieces to personalize it. It came out great!
                        <br/>
                        An idea to get chip wrappers...I work at an elementary school and the kids in my classroom are saving all their chip bags for me! They love the idea that they are recycling, and I am bringing in the chains to show them as I go along. I will probably make a bag and then donate it for a school auction. So check your local schools and ask them to recycle! (After I make one with chip wrappers I might ask the kids to save their capri sun pouches and try that next...)

                        Dear Mandy,
                        <br/>
                        I'm really not sure why your chains are gapping when you sew them together. Where are the gaps?? Make sure you sew on the inside and outside of each row. Also, make sure you are putting the rows together with a positive and negative together as described in the instructions.
                        <br/>
                        If anyone else has any suggestions or comments on what might help Mandy... please feel free give suggestions.

                        Good luck....

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-6209387215531612642">
                       <p>
                        I love these instructions! I made a purse for each of my girls. One is made entirely out of Cheetos wrappers, one is made from just about any kind of food wrapper we had available! You really start to pay attention to how stuff is packaged, and you start realizing how much stuff you've been sending to the landfill when you do one of these. I join my rows together using "gimp," that flat plastic stuff kids use to make lanyards. It's strong, flat, flexible and I don't need to use a needle. I do have to use a needle and thread for the zipper, of course. I make mine 9 rows high and the handle 2 rows thick. I'm having trouble joining the handles on the ends in a way that isn't going to come apart. I think I'm missing a step there. Might make the handle out of something else the next time. I would love to donate one of these to a school or church fundraiser. I'm going to try to figure out how to do a basket instead of a purse.
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-8408964432151669954">
                       <p>
                        Last fall, I discovered candywrapper purses while shopping in Burlington, Ontario. The sales person told me what the technique was called, and when I googled it I came upon your website.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I starting making the purses last fall and have made 20 so far and showed 30 people to make them, all proceeds go to charity. I prepare kits and the students choose the charity where the proceeds go to. So far I have raised 1,200$.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        My son created a website for me and I was hoping that I could use your instructions or mention your link, I need to post them in French and English.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I work as a secretary in a London, Ontario French high school, and have been teaching our students, and our community. I send purses to silent auctions for non-profit organizations (cancer society, foodbanks, local schools, youth and women services).
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        Hoping to hear from you soon, thank you again for helping me create such fun fundraising opportunities!

                      </dt>
                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-6848425237291389695">
                       <p>
                        Yesterday I set up a table in a flea market to sell some of my candy wrapper purses. Many people came by and looked at the purses. One person that came by was an older gentleman. He said that he had made items out of cigarette wrappers when he was in elelmentary school. I asked him if he was just making the chains and he said no. He said they were taught this craft in school and that they made all kinds of things(baskets, purses,belts) The interesting thing was that the gentleman said that he was in his eighties! He said that they were learning this craft in the thirties!
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I was wondering if anyone knows how old this craft is and where if began. I am always amazed at how you can take small pieces of paper and make strong, durable items out of them.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        June 7, 2009 6:19 AM
                       </p>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-9121386162385358793">
                       <p>
                        This response is to the last comment on how to make the bags straight across the top instead of pointed.  The bags that you see that look like the wrapper bags but are straight across the top are actually woved just like you would make a basket.  I would assume to your research basket making and use the wrappers for your material.  The other option would be to make the rows like I made the belt and sew those rows together.  Hope that answers your question.
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-716529596827644994">
                       <p>
                        Thanks to your wonderful instructions and the suggestions made by other on this blog, I have began make my own purse from the Sunday Comics using packing tape.  I secured the tape with the sticky side up to one end of my table, pulled it the length of my table, layed my cut papers on top and then cut them apart.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I cut my "needle" out of the top of a plastic coffee can lid, and used dental floss to sew the rounds together. When I tie a new piece of floss on, I tie a few knots with long tails, pull them tight, tie again, pull and again if necessary until it stops slipping and is tight.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I sewed the botton together after two rounds.  First, because I wanted to make sure I could make it work before I put lots of work into the project.  Second, I though I would have more working room as I sewed. Once I got the hang of it, it was not so hard.  With the dental floss, I was able to pull it together without  breaking the thread or tearing my folds.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I am concerned about putting the zipper in.  If I can't get it to work, I will try something else.  Maybe a flap?
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        What I have do so far is so darn cute.  I just waiting for the Sunday Comics to finish it.
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-2080045331017821271">
                       <p>
                        I am just trying my first bag.  I am going to make a small cosmetic size first.  I have the strips done. I asked on freecycle for some unused zippers. I got two bunches for someones closet and will be truly making these as a recycling project.  My second project is going to be a bigger bag with the Initials of some one on it.  I have planned a pattern on paper.  It will start with several rows of multi wrappers and then 17 rows of silver with the pattern of a single color wrapper in set spots to spell the initials PHS.  It took an hour or so to plan and draw the pattern out with crayons and graph paper. I have made paper tag (out of christmas cards from this year) and oldbread twist ties.  On the tag I am labelling the row number so I can keep them inorder to sew them together.  I am going to sew the first bag before I attempt the big bag.  I will show some pics when done. karen
                       </p>

                       said...
                      </dt>
                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-219874086040711230">
                       <p>
                        Here are are few more answers to some of your questions:
                        <br/>
                        1.  Do you have to make a needle like mine?  NO, You can use a paperclip if you want.  One person said they used the plastic from a coffee can lid or maybe pringles lid would work also.
                        <br/>
                        2.  Can you use regular sewing cotton thread?  If you pull the thread as hard as you can and it breaks, don't use it!  If the thread won't break, that's the thread to use.  Doesn't matter what kind of thread it is as long as it won't break because I tug mine really hard when sewing the purse together.
                        <br/>
                        3.  How do you make rows sturdier so wrappers don't unfold?  Sorry to say but if your wrappers are unfolding then your doing something wrong.  I've broken wrappers by pulling to hard on my thread but there is no way they can unfold then your sewing the rows together.
                        <br/>
                        4.  How long does it take to make a purse?  For the little coin purses, my guess is 8 - 12 hours.  For the purse, my guess is 40 plus hours.  Remember.....this is a pure guess.  For the square bottom purse,  to many to every want to make two of them, lol.
                        <br/>
                        5.  Do you need permission to sell the purses you make?  Heck NO, you sell as many as your fingers will allow you to make.  Please don't copy, sell or reprint the instructions.
                        <br/>
                        6.  My rows have gaps and are week as per one writer.  I hate to say it again but then your doing something wrong or pull your string tighter so you don't ever see the string!!
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-1820286939579989370">
                       <p>
                        How do you make an item that gradually slopes out (like a bowl) or in (like a vase)? How do I match up the links if the chains are different lengths?
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I'm having trouble with wrappers and labels of different weights and quality of plastic. The wrappers from soda bottles are my favorite because they have such bright colors, but they tear easily, and the tight stitching crumples them. When I use tape to reinforce them, they are thicker than some of the other labels and don't lay evenly.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I've been experimenting with types of paper to bulk up a thin label. Tracing and tissue paper were too slippery, and regular copier paper was too thick. I'm trying origami paper now, although there is a lot of waste since it only comes in small squares.
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I bought a roll of self-adhesive laminate at an art store and it works very well instead of the tape (for some reason I'm just hopeless with tape dispensers).
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        I am having a blast with this. My first effort is a mish-mosh of colors, but I'm going to try more sober designs next and use dull laminate for a matte finish.
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-282618333697448800">
                       <p>
                        Dear Eve,
                        <br/>
                        To answer your question on how to make your purse slope up.  Each row that you add has such a gradual increase that when your adding rows it's not really noticeable until your completely finished.  Just keep pulling the thread tight when you add rows to prevent gapping.  I also agree with you about the wrapper from soda bottles being thin but I also love to use them.  That is when you must add a piece of newspaper or magazine page to the inside of the piece before you fold.  If you have a few pieces in your rows of different weighted paper, you won't be able to find them when your completely finished with your project.
                        <br/>
                        I have torn a few of my chain links when I sewed some projects together and had to go in a fix one link piece....what a nightmare but I went about it like I was joining a row together.  It just takes A LOT of patience.  Best of luck to you and all your projects.
                        <br/>
                        Mylinda
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                       <p>
                        Mylinda,
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        Thank you! for working so hard to figure these out, and then sharing with everyone.
                        <br/>
                        I eagerly await instructions for the flat-bottom bag.
                        <br/>
                        I feel a little sad when people post about covering paper in tape or buying plastic banners to make the purses.  The purses are cool for many reasons, including that find a use for something that's otherwise garbage.  Buying packing tape, which I'm sure is made with many weird chemicals, seems contrary to the project's green sensibilities.  I think if we put out to our friends/communities that we are looking for chip/candy bags we'll get more than we need.  I have also found many lying by the side of the road.

                       <p>
                        Heidi, I know you say you are using the correct dimensions so I don't have a clue what you are doing wrong.  My guess is, the first fold is not the long edge or long side. When you make the first fold in half, fold it the long way, not the short way.  If you still have trouble send me an e-mail and send you more pictures.

                        good luck. Mylinda

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-1644398752445018276">
                       <p>
                        could it be that your rows are not the same way up? - the direction of the folds needs to be in the same direction - see here http://shesewsonsunday.blogspot.com/2010/02/different-candy-wrapper-patterns.html
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        the yellow row should be turned the other way uo so that all the outer folds go the same way
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        may be?  or maybe its the joining fold - so check that is the same direction
                        <br/>
                        <br/>
                        hope that helps and happy folding
                       </p>
                      </dd>

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-4537442936609056371">
                       <p>
                        Hi, I'm in the process of making my first candy wrapper purse (or bag, I should say)! Your blog was very helpful Mylinda, thank you! I have already made most of the body of the purse, and I am quite ready to be done with it finally. Anyway, I was wondering if Mylinda or anyone else has ever lined the inside of their purse? I have not duct taped any of my pieces, since I have been using granola, chip, and other mostly waterproof wrappers. I wanted to make this bag suitable to carry a spiral bound school notebook, so for extra dryness precaution I was thinking of using umbrella fabric to line the inside of the bag... as well as make the bottom and handles! My family has helped me think up of a few possible techniques to achieve this without the umbrella fabric looking like a misshapen lump sticking out the end of the candy wrapper body, but we're not experienced crafters so I was wondering if anyone else had an idea?
                        <br/>
                        -K

                      <dd class="comment-body" id="Blog1_cmt-6405934943385164337">
                       <p>
                        Thank you for posting  this!  I crochet bags but this looks like a lot of fun to try for a change.  My boyfriend says the guys in prison pay people for their chip bag and candy wrappers.  They make things like this and also little cars where the doors open and other things and get a couple hundred for their art work!  wow.  Who would have thought.  lol  I can't wait to try this.  My dad is a fallen firefighter and we get the Fireman's Grapevine - the LAFD magazine.  I can't bear to throw away any of the magazines, but now I can put them to a great use!  I think they would make beautiful bags and clutches!  Thank you again!
                       </p>
